                                                                  5325 1451   42
                     GENERAL COMMENTS                             5325 1451   43
                                                                  5325 1451   44
     Resolved resonance parameters from an analysis of Mughabghab 5325 1451   45
 (Mu81) were used with a multi-level Breit-Wigner representation  5325 1451   46
 to represent the total, elastic, and capture data up to an       5325 1451   47
 incident neutron energy of 1 keV.                                5325 1451   48
     The evaluation above the resonance region (E > 1 keV) is     5325 1451   49
 based on a theoretical analysis using the SCAT2 optical model    5325 1451   50
 code (Be78), the COMNUC (Du70) and GNASH (Yo77, Ar88) Hauser-    5325 1451   51
 Feshbach statistical theory codes, the DWUCK (Ku70) distorted-   5325 1451   52
 wave Born approximation code, and the ECIS (Ra72) coupled-       5325 1451   53
 channel deformed optical model code.                             5325 1451   54
                                                                  5325 1451   55
   OPTICAL MODEL POTENTIAL:  The spherical optical model          5325 1451   56
 potential of Yamamuro (Ya90), which utilizes Walter's (Wa85)     5325 1451   57
 potential above 20 MeV, was utilized with slight modification    5325 1451   58
 at low energies, similar to Ya88. For protons, the potential of  5325 1451   59
 Perey (Pe63) was modified to include an energy-dependent term    5325 1451   60
 in the surface imaginary potential. The alpha potential used by  5325 1451   61
 Arthur and Young in Fe calculations (Ar80) was adopted for alpha 5325 1451   62
 particles. The above potentials were used to supply transmission 5325 1451   63
 coefficients for neutrons, protons, and alpha particles in the   5325 1451   64
 Hauser-Feshbach statistical calculations.  Of course, all the    5325 1451   65
 neutron cross sections depend on the potentials through the      5325 1451   66
 transmission coefficients.  It was necessary only to adjust the  5325 1451   67
 the neutron total and capture cross sections to improve agree-   5325 1451   68
 ment with experimental data. The neutron potential was used to   5325 1451   69
 obtain all the shape elastic components of the neutron elastic   5325 1451   70
 scattering angular distributions, as well as the compound elas-  5325 1451   71
 tic and inelastic scattering angular distribution components.    5325 1451   72
                                                                  5325 1451   73
   DIRECT REACTION ANALYSIS:  The coupled-channel calcula-        5325 1451   74
 tions of Matoba (Ma75) for Te126 were repeated with ECIS in      5325 1451   75
 order to verify the importance of vibrational states and to con- 5325 1451   76
 firm the validity of using simple DWBA calculations. The defor-  5325 1451   77
 mation parameters beta(l=2,J=2+) and beta(l=3,J=3-) from Ma75,   5325 1451   78
 together with B(E2) and B(E3) values for I-127 in Nuclear Data   5325 1451   79
 Sheets (Ha82), were used to infer deformation parameters for     5325 1451   80
 I-127 levels. The E2 strength was distributed among known levels 5325 1451   81
 in I-127; the E3 strength was distributed among 5 arbitarily     5325 1451   82
 assumed negative parity levels between Ex=1.3 and 2.1 MeV in     5325 1451   83
 I-127. The deformation parameters from the above analysis were   5325 1451   84
 used in DWBA calculations with DWUCK to provide cross section    5325 1451   85
 and angular distributions for the discrete I127(n,n') reactions  5325 1451   86
 to relevant levels in I-127. The compound nucleus reaction       5325 1451   87
 cross section was decreased appropriately for the direct         5325 1451   88
 reaction components.                                             5325 1451   89
                                                                  5325 1451   90
   HAUSER-FESHBACH STATISTICAL CALCULATIONS:  The GNASH code      5325 1451   91
 (Yo77,Ar88) was used for all Hauser-Feshbach statistical theory  5325 1451   92
 calculations between 0.001 and 30 MeV. Width fluctuation cor-    5325 1451   93
 rections were obtained from the COMNUC code (Du70), which        5325 1451   94
 utilizes the model of Moldauer (Mo76). Preequilibrium correc-    5325 1451   95
 tions are carried out in GNASH with the exciton model of Kalbach 5325 1451   96
 (Ka77,Ka85). Discrete level data were obtained from nuclear data 5325 1451   97
 sheets (Ha82); continuum level densities were represented with   5325 1451   98
 the Gilbert-Cameron (Gi65) model using the Cook parameters       5325 1451   99
 (Co67). Particle transmission coefficients were obtained from    5325 1451  100
 the optical model calculations described above. Transmission     5325 1451  101
 coefficients for gamma rays were calculated using the Brink-     5325 1451  102
 Axel model (Br55,Ax62). Normalization of the gamma-ray strength  5325 1451  103
 function was carried out using the compilation of Mughabghab     5325 1451  104
 (Mu81).  Calculations were carried out for all reactions that    5325 1451  105
 produce neutrons, protons, alpha particles, or gamma rays for    5325 1451  106
 incident neutron energies between 1 keV and 30 MeV. The RECOIL   5325 1451  107
 code (Ma84) by MacFarlane was used to analyze and unfold the     5325 1451  108
 GNASH output for representation in ENDF/B MF=6 format. Angular   5325 1451  109
 distribution systematics by Kalbach (Ka88) were used to describe 5325 1451  110
 angular distributions for continuum particles, as well as dis-   5325 1451  111
 crete reactions where direct reaction data were lacking.         5325 1451  112
                                                                  5325 1451  113

 MT=1  Total Cross Section.                                       5325 1451  128
   1 keV to 14 MeV, optical model calculation adjusted to         5325 1451  129
     agree with bulk of experimental data.  Below 100 keV,        5325 1451  130
     smoothly joined with resonance range.  From 0.1 to 3 MeV,    5325 1451  131
     data of Ta68, Mi52, Bo49 emphasized. From 3 to 14 MeV,       5325 1451  132
     mainly Fo71 data used. Near 30 MeV, exp. data of De61 used   5325 1451  133
     to adjust optical model calculations.                        5325 1451  134
 MT=2 Elastic Scattering Cross Section.                           5325 1451  135
   1 keV to 30 MeV, obtained by subtracting all nonelastic cross  5325 1451  136
     sections from total. Essentially equal to combination of     5325 1451  137
     shape elastic cross section from SCAT2 and compound elastic  5325 1451  138
     cross section from COMNUC calculation. Optical model pot.    5325 1451  139
     and other parameters were taken from the analysis described  5325 1451  140
     above.                                                       5325 1451  141

   37, 91, 649, and 849 were calculated with the GNASH reaction   5325 1451  195
